       <!-- .entry-header --> 
       <div class="entry-content single"> 
        <p>Now you can translate your Microsoft Office documents with Microsoft Translator – right within Office! You can translate words, phrases, or even your entire document, through the Research task pane. We blogged about setting this up manually for <a href="http://blogs.msdn.com/translation/archive/2008/08/06/office-document-translation.aspx" mce_href="http://blogs.msdn.com/translation/archive/2008/08/06/office-document-translation.aspx">Office 2007</a> or <a href="http://blogs.msdn.com/translation/archive/2008/08/11/office-2003-setup-instructions.aspx" mce_href="http://blogs.msdn.com/translation/archive/2008/08/11/office-2003-setup-instructions.aspx">Office 2003</a> previously - now it's really easy! </p>
        <p>&nbsp;</p> 
        <p> This works for both Microsoft Office 2003 and 2007. The current default in Microsoft Office is WorldLingo – this installer will update your task pane to use Microsoft Translator as the default translator for the languages we provide. </p>
        <p>&nbsp;</p> 
        <p> <a href="http://go.microsoft.com/?linkid=9660314" mce_href="http://go.microsoft.com/?linkid=9660314">Download the installer</a> now and let us know what you think over in the <a href="http://go.microsoft.com/?linkid=9656020" mce_href="http://go.microsoft.com/?linkid=9656020">Forum</a>! </p> 
       </div>

         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/3651e719491c63d4424134d66fe53db9?s=56&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/3651e719491c63d4424134d66fe53db9?s=112&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn">Takako Aikawa</cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-10773"> April 20, 2009 at 12:33 pm</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>In Office 2007, go to Review and you’ll see Translate button in the ribbon. &nbsp;Click Translate and you’ll see the Research task pane. &nbsp;Choose [Translate] under [All Reference Books] and then, click on [Translation options]. &nbsp;Translation Options box shows up and there, you’ll see Microsoft Translator option for the language pairs [Arabic-&gt;English/English-&gt;Arabic, Chinese-&gt;English/English-&gt;Chinese, etc.]. &nbsp;For the languages pairs that Microsoft Translator currently accommodates, go to: <a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://www.microsofttranslator.com/">http://www.microsofttranslator.com/</a>. &nbsp;Hope that you can find Microsoft Translator in your Office.</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=10773#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-10773&quot;, &quot;10773&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Takako Aikawa">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment byuser comment-author-christw odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-14093"> 
        <div id="div-comment-14093" class="comment-body"> 
         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://i1.social.s-msft.com/profile/u/avatar.jpg?displayname=Chris+Wendt&amp;size=extralarge&amp;version=645801fb-1121-461a-be2a-81d7a3ecbdcf" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn"><a href="https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/profile/Chris+Wendt" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Chris Wendt</a></cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-14093"> December 24, 2009 at 6:49 am</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hello Natalie,</p> 
         <p>jhere are the steps to produce a completely translated document with Microsoft Translator: — Choose Translate from the menu</p> 
         <p>– Choose your languages</p> 
         <p>– Click on the little green arrow that says "Translate the whole document". This will open the translated document in your browser. – – Using the icons at the top, choose "Translation with hover original", the one on the right.</p> 
         <p>– Click somewhere in the translated text.</p> 
         <p>– Press Ctrl-A to select the whole translation.</p> 
         <p>– Press Ctrl-C to copy teh selection to the clipboard.</p> 
         <p>– Open a new document and press Ctrl-V to insert the complete text.</p> 
         <p>Chris Wendt</p> 
         <p>Microsoft Translator</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=14093#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-14093&quot;, &quot;14093&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to christw">Reply</a>

         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-14143"> December 27, 2009 at 4:10 am</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Download the Microsoft Translator installer for Microsoft Office</p> 
         <p>Now you can translate your Microsoft Office documents with Microsoft Translator – right within Office! You can translate words, phrases, or even your entire document, through the Research task pane. We blogged about setting this up manually for Office 2007 or Office 2003 previously – now it’s really easy! </p> 
         <p>This works for both Microsoft Office 2003 and 2007. The current default in Microsoft Office is WorldLingo – this installer will update your task pane to use Microsoft Translator as the default translator for the languages we provide. </p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=14143#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-14143&quot;, &quot;14143&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to Nasser">Reply</a>

         <p>How do you type accents and so on in Microsoft translator?</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=16813#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-16813&quot;, &quot;16813&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to robkawa9">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment byuser comment-author-mtteam bypostauthor odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-16823"> 
        <div id="div-comment-16823" class="comment-body"> 
         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://i1.social.s-msft.com/profile/u/avatar.jpg?displayname=Microsoft+Translator&amp;size=extralarge&amp;version=257a61df-059c-4cee-9bba-949338a34554" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn"><a href="https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/profile/Microsoft+Translator" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Microsoft Translator</a></cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-16823"> June 14, 2010 at 7:27 am</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hi Rob,</p> 
         <p>if you are normally using the English (United States) keyboard, the easiest is to use the "United States-International" keyboard, which allows you to create accents using new dead keys that look like the accent. For instance ç by typing , followed by c, and ä by typing " followed by a. To use this keyboard, visit the Reagion and Language item in the Windows control panel, choose the tab for "Keyboards and Languages" and then "Change keyboards". You can have multiple keyboards installed at once, but using "the United Stats-International" keyboard exclusively is possible, and works well for me. You just need to remember to hit the space bar wherever you want the "accent" alone.</p> 
         <p>Chris Wendt</p> 
         <p>Microsoft Translator</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=16823#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-16823&quot;, &quot;16823&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to MTTeam">Reply</a>

         </div> 
         <p>Hi Robert,</p> 
         <p>Regarding the display of Chinese characters, this might be your Browser issue.</p> 
         <p>To nail down the problem, check to see whether you can see Chinese characters inside your Research pane (i.e., the right-hand side pane in Word) when you translate selected texts into Chinese. &nbsp;</p> 
         <p>If you can see the Chinese characters there, then it’s your Browser issue.</p> 
         <p>Not sure which Browser you use but if it’s IE, you might want to check Encoding under the Page button on IE.</p> 
         <p>I’ll put some helpful links on how to use the Translate feature in Word below, just in case.</p> 
         <p><a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://blogs.msdn.com/b/translation/archive/2008/08/06/office-document-translation.aspx">blogs.msdn.com/…/office-document-translation.aspx</a></p> 
         <p><a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://www.howtogeek.com/howto/microsoft-office/translate-selected-text-in-microsoft-word-2007/">http://www.howtogeek.com/…/translate-selected-text-in-microsoft-word-2007</a></p> 
         <p>Hope that this helps.</p>

       <li class="comment byuser comment-author-mtteam bypostauthor odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-17043"> 
        <div id="div-comment-17043" class="comment-body"> 
         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://i1.social.s-msft.com/profile/u/avatar.jpg?displayname=Microsoft+Translator&amp;size=extralarge&amp;version=257a61df-059c-4cee-9bba-949338a34554" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn"><a href="https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/profile/Microsoft+Translator" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Microsoft Translator</a></cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-17043"> July 6, 2010 at 5:48 pm</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hi Douglas,</p> 
         <p>To find the Translate feature in Word 2007, do the following:</p> 
         <p>1. Highlight the text to be translated, then go to the Tools menu. &nbsp;Select the Language menu option and then the Translate submenu option. The Research Task Pane (on the right-hand side) will appear. &nbsp; (You can do the same by right-clicking and then select Translate.)</p> 
         <p>2. In the Translation section of the Research Task Pane, you will see the fields From and To. In the From field, select the language that you want to translate from. &nbsp;In the To field, select the language that you want to translate the selected text into.</p> 
         <p>3. Once the languages in the From and To fields are selected, click on the green arrow below the To field to translate the text.</p> 
         <p>You should be able to see the translation text(s) inside the Research Task pane.</p> 
         <p>Hope that this helps.</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=17043#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-17043&quot;, &quot;17043&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to MTTeam">Reply</a>
         </div> 
        </div> </li>

         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-19003"> June 6, 2011 at 9:15 am</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hi Mary,</p> 
         <p>I thought I posted my comment(s) last week in response to your question. &nbsp;Looks like it didn’t go through.</p> 
         <p>To create a translation document with picture(s), use selected-text(s) translation instead of a whole document translation.</p> 
         <p>Basically, you select your text(s); translate them into the language you want to see; and insert the translated sentence(s) into the document. &nbsp;You can get detailed information on the selected text translation at the following sites.</p> 
         <p><a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://blogs.msdn.com/b/translation/archive/2008/08/06/office-document-translation.aspx">blogs.msdn.com/…/office-document-translation.aspx</a></p> 
         <p><a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://office.microsoft.com/en-us/word-help/translate-text-in-a-different-language-HA010354288.aspx?CTT=1">office.microsoft.com/…/translate-text-in-a-different-language-HA010354288.aspx</a></p> 
         <p>Hope that this is helpful. &nbsp;Thanks. &nbsp;Takako (Microsoft Translator team)</p>

       <li class="comment byuser comment-author-mtteam bypostauthor even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-19203"> 
        <div id="div-comment-19203" class="comment-body"> 
         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://i1.social.s-msft.com/profile/u/avatar.jpg?displayname=Microsoft+Translator&amp;size=extralarge&amp;version=257a61df-059c-4cee-9bba-949338a34554" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn"><a href="https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/profile/Microsoft+Translator" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Microsoft Translator</a></cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-19203"> August 15, 2011 at 6:33 pm</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hi Edward,</p> 
         <p>I'm assuming you mean our Text To Speech (TTS) option, which is available on our main site (<a rel="nofollow" target="_new" href="http://www.microsofttranslator.com">http://www.microsofttranslator.com</a>). &nbsp;When you translate from one language to another, if the target language (the one you're translating to) supports TTS, you will see a Speak button. &nbsp;When you press this button, you will hear the translation. Unfortunately, this option is not available in Office, but only on our main site and through our API.</p> 
         <p>I hope this answers your question.</p> 
         <p>Sincerely,</p> 
         <p>Will Lewis</p> 
         <p>Microsoft Translator</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=19203#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-19203&quot;, &quot;19203&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to MTTeam">Reply</a>

       <li class="comment byuser comment-author-mtteam bypostauthor even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-22263"> 
        <div id="div-comment-22263" class="comment-body"> 
         <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
          <img alt="" src="https://i1.social.s-msft.com/profile/u/avatar.jpg?displayname=Microsoft+Translator&amp;size=extralarge&amp;version=257a61df-059c-4cee-9bba-949338a34554" class="avatar avatar-56 photo" height="56" width="56"> 
          <cite class="fn"><a href="https://social.msdn.microsoft.com/profile/Microsoft+Translator" rel="external nofollow" class="url">Microsoft Translator</a></cite> 
          <span class="says">says:</span> 
         </div> 
         <div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
          <a href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/#comment-22263"> September 16, 2013 at 7:14 am</a> 
         </div> 
         <p>Hi Judith,</p> 
         <p>For a very short selection, Office shows a dictionary answer instead of translation. The dictionary answer indeed has no Insert button.</p> 
         <p>The way to change this is to turn off the dictionary. Visit “Translation options…” in the research pane, and uncheck “Use online dictionary”. That’ll fix Japanese. If you have local dictionaries (likely you do, for French and Spanish) you’ll need to disable them individually in that same dialog.</p> 
         <p>Let us know if that worked,</p> 
         <p>Your Microsoft Translator team</p> 
         <div class="reply">
          <a rel="nofollow" class="comment-reply-link" href="https://blogs.msdn.microsoft.com/translation/2009/04/16/download-the-microsoft-translator-installer-for-microsoft-office/?replytocom=22263#respond" onclick="return addComment.moveForm( &quot;div-comment-22263&quot;, &quot;22263&quot;, &quot;respond&quot;, &quot;603&quot; )" aria-label="Reply to MTTeam">Reply</a>

  <script>
		jQuery(window).load(function () {
			// Fix Bug #644092:MAS36: Page number
			jQuery('div.nav-links>a.page-numbers').each(function(){
				jQuery(this).attr('aria-label', 'Page ' + jQuery(this).html());
			});

			// Fix Bug #633981:MAS20B:  Talkback: Talkback announces link for Number of Comments as 'Number link'
			jQuery('span.comments-link>a').each(function () {
				var num = parseInt(jQuery(this).html());
				if (isNaN(num)) {
					return false;
				}
				var content = num + (num === 1 ? ' comment' : ' comments');
				jQuery(this).attr({
					'aria-label': content,
					'title': content
				});
			});


			jQuery('#search-option>div').each(function () {
				jQuery(this).attr('aria-label',jQuery('span.search-text',this).html());
			});

			// Fix Bug #671896:MAS40B :Inspect: Header: "Name" property is not descriptive for  "Microsoft | TechNet" link (logo).
			var currentHost = location.hostname;
			if (currentHost.indexOf('msdn') !== -1) {
				jQuery('#home-link').attr('aria-label','Microsoft Developer');
			} else if (currentHost.indexOf('technet') !== -1) {
				jQuery('#home-link').attr('aria-label','Microsoft Technet');
			}

			// Detect High Contrast Mode in non IE/Edge Browsers
			jQuery('html').css('background-image', 'url("data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAP///wAAACH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAICRAEAOw==")');
			if (jQuery('html').css('background-image') === 'none') {
				jQuery('html').attr('data-high-contrast', 'true');
			}

			// Fix Bug #670327:MAS40B: Inspect: Header: "Localized control type" property is incorrect for the header elements.
			// Fix Bug #683788:MAS40B: TalkBack: Header: For menu items in technet link menu bar, expand/collapse pattern available, is not announced by TalkBack 
			jQuery('#site-navigation>div>ul>li>a').attr('role', 'button').attr('aria-expanded', 'false').click(function () {
				if (jQuery(this).attr('aria-expanded') === 'true') {
					jQuery(this).attr('aria-expanded', 'false');
				} else {
					jQuery(this).attr('aria-expanded', 'true');
				}
			});

		});
	</script>
